<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Hurricane Maria</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."/><img alt="show/hide details" class="fr-toggle-arrow" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/arrow-down.png" style="display:none;"/></div>

<p><b>Hurricane Maria</b> was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_intense_tropical_cyclones#North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="List of the most intense tropical cyclones">tenth-most intense Atlantic hurricane on record</a>, the worst natural disaster in <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> in its recorded history, and the strongest hurricane to make landfall in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> since <a href="/wiki/1928_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1928 Atlantic hurricane season">1928</a>. The thirteenth <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named storm</a>, seventh <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a>, fourth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_hurricane" title="Major hurricane">major hurricane</a>, and the second Category 5 hurricane of the unusually active <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017 Atlantic hurricane season</a>, Maria caused catastrophic damage during its journey across the Northeastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> as the second most intense landfall and the costliest hurricane ever to hit the region. It was the third major hurricane in a row to threaten the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> with a direct strike or major impacts within two weeks, after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> caused catastrophic damage there and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Jose</a>, then a Category 4 hurricane, passed dangerously close just days after.</p>
<p>Originating from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> began monitoring on September 13, Maria developed into a tropical storm on September 16 east of the Lesser Antilles, with steady strengthening occurring. In remarkably favorable conditions for further development, on September 18, Maria underwent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explosive_intensification" title="Explosive intensification">explosive intensification</a>, doubling its sustained wind speed from 80 mph (130 km/h) to 160 mph (260 km/h), becoming a Category 5 hurricane, making the 2017 season the first since <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a> to feature two Category 5 hurricanes, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes#Systems" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">one of only six Atlantic hurricane seasons</a> to feature two or more Category 5 hurricanes in the satellite era. When Maria made landfall at this strength on <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, on the following day, it became the first Category 5 hurricane to strike Dominica, and made 2017 the second season (after 2007) to feature two hurricanes making landfall at Category 5 intensity. After briefly weakening to Category 4 status, Maria reintensified to attain peak winds of 175 mph (280 km/h) and a minimum central pressure of 908 mbar (hPa; 26.85 inHg), becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_intense_tropical_cyclones#North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="List of most intense tropical cyclones">tenth most intense Atlantic hurricane</a> on record. For 2017, this central pressure is the lowest worldwide thus far. Succeeding peak intensity, an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> caused Maria to weaken to a high-end Category 4 hurricane with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h) before making landfall in Puerto Rico, making Maria the strongest to hit the territory since the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 San Felipe hurricane</a>. Maria had the lowest central pressure of any hurricane to make landfall in the United States (including locations outside of the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">Lower 48</a>) since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">Hurricane Camille</a> in 1969, and the lowest pressure ever recorded in Puerto Rico.</p>
<p>As of October 1, the hurricane has caused at least 78 deaths: 30 in <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, 5 in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, 3 in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, 34 in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, 1 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>, and 3 in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>. Initial assessments indicate catastrophic damage to Dominica, which suffered an island-wide communication blackout. The islands of Guadeloupe and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> also endured widespread flooding, damaged roofs and uprooted trees. Puerto Rico has suffered catastrophic damage, including destruction of its previously damaged electrical grid. Total losses from the hurricane are estimated at around $91 billion (2017 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">USD</a>), mostly in Puerto Rico, making Maria's cost comparable to that of previous Hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Harvey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consumerinfoline_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-consumerinfoline-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insuredlosses_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-insuredlosses-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2290" data-file-width="3000" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/275px-Maria_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/413px-Maria_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/550px-Maria_2017_track.png 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) began monitoring two <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical waves</a> on September 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The easternmost wave quickly spun up into what would become <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Lee" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Lee</a>, while the western one continued moving generally west. With generally favorable conditions in the disturbance's path, development into a tropical cyclone seemed likely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> During those two days the disturbance became better organized,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and by September 16, <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">convective banding</a> became established around a poorly organized circulation. As the system was an imminent threat to land despite the center not being well-defined, the NHC initiated advisories on it as "Potential Tropical Cyclone Fifteen" at 15:00 UTC, in accordance with a policy change enacted at the start of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-D1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> A mid-level <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> anchored north of the disturbance steered it generally west-northwest into a region highly favorable for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">further development</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">Sea surface temperatures</a> of 84 °F (29 °C), low <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, and ample moisture were anticipated to foster strengthening to hurricane-status before the system reached the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-D1-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D4_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-D4-8">[8]</a></sup> As the disturbance continued to grow increasingly well-defined throughout the day, it was later upgraded to a moderate-range tropical storm – based on satellite estimates – at 21:00 UTC that day, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">receiving the name</a> <i>Maria</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> At this time, Maria was situated 620 mi (1,000 km) east-southeast of the Lesser Antilles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

<th>10</th>
<td><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Maria</a></td>

<td>908</td>
<td>26.81</td>

<tr class="small">

</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> and favorable <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> developed atop the center of circulation, which enabled Maria to become further organized throughout the early morning hours of September 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D4_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-D4-8">[8]</a></sup> After a brief intrusion of dry air exposed the circulation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> a convective burst occurred over the center and intensification resumed. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" title="Hurricane Hunters">Hurricane Hunters</a> investigating the system observed surface winds of 74 mph (119 km/h) and a formative <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> feature. Accordingly, the NHC upgraded Maria to hurricane status at 21:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Expansion of the central dense overcast and an increasingly complete eyewall signaled steady intensification throughout the overnight of September 17–18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Considerable <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> activity was identified within the hurricane's core early on September 18 and statistical models indicated a high probability of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Explosive strengthening took place shortly thereafter, with aircraft reconnaissance finding surface winds of 120 mph (195 km/h) and a central pressure of 959 mbar (hPa; 28.32 inHg), making Maria a Category 3 hurricane on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a>, and hence a major hurricane. Additionally, radar data revealed a well-defined 12 mi (19 km) wide eye.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The eye contracted slightly to 9 mi (14 km) as intensification continued, and the system reached Category 4 strength by 21:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="616" data-file-width="693" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/220px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/330px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/440px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Radar imagery of Hurricane Maria from Puerto Rico at 09:36 UTC (5:36 a.m. local time), shortly before it stopped transmitting data.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rapid intensification culminated late on September 18, with Maria achieving Category 5 status just 15 mi (25 km) east-southeast of Dominica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Hurricane Hunters observed surface winds of 160 mph (260 km/h) and a pressure of 925 mbar (hPa; 27.32 inHg) at this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Maria made <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfall</a> in Dominica at 01:15 UTC on September 19,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominica_landfall_TCU_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dominica_landfall_TCU-20">[20]</a></sup> becoming the first Category 5 hurricane on record to strike the island nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Interaction with the mountains of Dominica imparted slight weakening of the hurricane to Category 4; however, once over the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> Maria regained Category 5 intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Additional strengthening took place as the storm tracked northwest toward <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Despite the formation of concentric eyewalls—the larger one spanning 25 to 35 mi (40 to 56 km) and the smaller only 5 mi (8.0 km), signalling the start of an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>—the inner violent core remained undisrupted through the afternoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Maria attained its peak intensity around 04:00 UTC on September 20, roughly 30 mi (45 km) south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Croix" title="St. Croix">St. Croix</a>. Sustained winds reached 175 mph (280 km/h) and its central pressure bottomed out at 908 mbar (hPa; 26.85 inHg); this ranks it as the tenth-strongest Atlantic hurricane since reliable records began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/220px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/330px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/440px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Infrared loop of Hurricane Maria passing St. Croix, Vieques, and landfalling on Puerto Rico on the morning of September 20</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The hurricane made its closest approach to St. Croix around 05:00 UTC on September 20, passing within 20 mi (30 km) of the island; the storm's outer eyewall lashed the island while the more violent inner eye remained offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Hours later, around 08:00 UTC, the outer eyewall struck <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vieques" title="Vieques">Vieques</a>, an island off the eastern coast of Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> By this time, the outer eye became dominant as the inner one decayed, and the eyewall replacement cycle caused Maria to weaken to Category 4 strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Maria made landfall just south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yabucoa" title="Yabucoa">Yabucoa</a>, Puerto Rico, around 10:15 UTC with sustained winds of 155 mph (250 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> making it the strongest to hit the island since the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 San Felipe Segundo hurricane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Maria maintained a general west-northwest course across Puerto Rico, emerging over the Atlantic Ocean shortly before 18:00 UTC. Interaction with the mountainous terrain resulted in substantial weakening; sustained winds fell to 110 mph (175 km/h) and the central pressure rose to 957 mbars (hPa; 28.26 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> With favorable environmental conditions, Maria steadily reorganized as it moved away from Puerto Rico. A large eye, 45 mi (75 km) wide, developed with deep convection blossoming around it. Early on September 21, the system regained Category 3 intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, cooler waters <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">stirred up</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> two weeks prior limited Maria's reorganization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> During the afternoon of September 21, the system traversed the <a href="/wiki/Navidad_Bank" title="Navidad Bank">Navidad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Bank" title="Silver Bank">Silver</a> banks north of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Wave_shoaling" title="Wave shoaling">shoaling</a> from the region's shallow waters temporarily interfered with measurements of surface winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Convection around the storm's eye deepened and its eye became better defined that night, and the hurricane reached a tertiary peak with sustained winds of 125 mph (205 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> An increase in southwesterly wind shear prompted gradual weakening of the hurricane, starting with restriction of banding features and later degradation of the eyewall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Late on September 22, the hurricane turned north-northwest as it reached the western periphery of the ridge previously steering it northwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Maria fluctuated in organization throughout September 23, with its eye periodically clearing and becoming cloud-filled; it maintained Category 3 hurricane strength during this phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Despite a decreasing central pressure, the storm finally weakened to Category 2 strength early on September 24. Hurricane Hunters observed flight-level winds of 116 to 135 mph (187 to 217 km/h); however, surface wind returns by the NOAA's <a href="/wiki/Microwave_radiometer" title="Microwave radiometer">Stepped-Frequency Microwave Radiometer</a> were only 90 mph (150 km/h). This indicated below-average mixing down of winds aloft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D34_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-D34-44">[44]</a></sup> By this time, Maria's trajectory shifted almost due north between the aforementioned ridge and a <a href="/wiki/Block_(meteorology)#Cut-off_highs_and_lows" title="Block (meteorology)">cut-off low</a> over the eastern <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D34_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-D34-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Weakening accelerated later on September 24 into September 25, as the hurricane traversed a cold wake—with sea surface temperatures of 75–77 °F (24–25 °C)—created by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose</a> a week prior. Maria degraded to Category 1 strength during this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Early on September 25, Maria's structure changed dramatically as its inner-core collapsed. The low-level circulation became exposed to the northwest, and most of the deep convection shifted to the eastern half of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Maria further weakened into a tropical storm during the late afternoon of September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> However, a sustained convective burst resulted in Maria's winds increasing to hurricane-force once again on September 27,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> with banding features evident on the eastern part of the circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Despite this, northwesterly wind shear continued to impinge on the storm, and Maria once again weakened to a tropical storm early on September 28. Simultaneously, Maria began to accelerate to the east-northeast as it became embedded into the mid-latitude westerlies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Gradually weakening, Maria soon began to move over sea surface temperatures of 73 °F (23 °C) and below, causing most of its convection to dissipate. Late on September 30, Maria transitioned into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> During the next couple of days, Maria's remnant accelerated towards the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, while rapidly weakening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_1_weather_map_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-October_1_weather_map-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_2_weather_map_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-October_2_weather_map-53">[53]</a></sup> Maria's remnants later crossed the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> into the western Mediterranean Sea, before being absorbed by another frontal system later on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_3_weather_map_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-October_3_weather_map-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Navy_Helps_Evacuate_Military_From_U.S._Virgin_Islands_Ahead_of_Hurricane_Maria.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The U.S. Navy helps evacuate military personnel from the U.S. Virgin Islands, ahead of Hurricane Maria</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon the initiation of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC)'s first advisories for the system that would become Tropical Storm Maria on the morning of September 16, the government of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> issued tropical storm watches for the islands of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lucia" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a> issued a tropical storm watch for its citizens, and the government of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> issued a similar watch for <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public_advisory_1_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_1-55">[55]</a></sup> Barbados would later that day declare a tropical storm watch for its citizens and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public_advisory_1a_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_1a-56">[56]</a></sup> The government of <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> issued Hurricane watches for the islands of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Kitts" title="St. Kitts">St. Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> by the time of the NHC's second advisory which declared Maria a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-public_advisory_2_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_2-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washington_post_1_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-washington_post_1-58">[58]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> activated the <a href="/wiki/International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters" title="International Charter on Space and Major Disasters">International Charter on Space and Major Disasters</a> for humanitarian satellite coverage on the 20th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominican_Republic_Activates_the_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dominican_Republic_Activates_the_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Still recovering from Hurricane Irma two weeks prior, approximately 80,000 remained without power as Maria approached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Electric_Power_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority">Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority</a> (PREPA) struggled with increasing debt, reaching $9 billion even before the hurricanes prompting them to file for bankruptcy. Furthermore, the company lost 30 percent of its employees since 2012. Aging infrastructure across the island makes the grid more susceptible to damage from storms; the median age of PREPA power plants is 44 years. Inadequate safety also plagues the company and local newspapers frequently describe poor maintenance and outdated controls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evacuation orders were issued in Puerto Rico in advance of Maria, and officials announced that 450 shelters would open in the afternoon of September 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> As of September 19, at least 2,000 people in Puerto Rico had sought shelter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland_United_States">Mainland United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mainland United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As Maria approached the coast of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and threatened to bring tropical storm conditions, a storm surge warning was issued for the coast between <a href="/wiki/Ocracoke_Inlet" title="Ocracoke Inlet">Ocracoke Inlet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a>, while a storm surge watch was issued for the <a href="/wiki/Pamlico_Sound" title="Pamlico Sound">Pamlico Sound</a>, the lower <a href="/wiki/Neuse_River" title="Neuse River">Neuse River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Alligator_River_(North_Carolina)" title="Alligator River (North Carolina)">Alligator River</a> on the morning of September 26. A state of emergency was declared by officials in <a href="/wiki/Dare_County,_North_Carolina" title="Dare County, North Carolina">Dare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyde_County,_North_Carolina" title="Hyde County, North Carolina">Hyde</a> counties, while visitors were ordered to evacuate <a href="/wiki/Hatteras_Island" title="Hatteras Island">Hatteras</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocracoke_Island" title="Ocracoke Island">Ocracoke</a> islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup> Ferry service between <a href="/wiki/Ocracoke,_North_Carolina" title="Ocracoke, North Carolina">Ocracoke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Island,_North_Carolina" title="Cedar Island, North Carolina">Cedar Island</a> was suspended the evening of September 25, and remained suspended on September 26 and 27, due to rough seas, while ferry service between Ocracoke and Hatteras Island was suspended on September 26 and 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver2_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver2-65">[65]</a></sup> The port in <a href="/wiki/Morehead_City,_North_Carolina" title="Morehead City, North Carolina">Morehead City</a> was closed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a> on the morning of September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup> Schools in Dare County closed on September 26 and 27, while schools in <a href="/wiki/Carteret_County,_North_Carolina" title="Carteret County, North Carolina">Carteret</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyrrell_County,_North_Carolina" title="Tyrrell County, North Carolina">Tyrrell</a> counties, along with Ocracoke Island, dismissed early on September 26, in anticipation of high winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver2_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver2-65">[65]</a></sup> Schools in <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">Currituck County</a> were closed on September 27, due to high winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver2_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver2-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_in_the_Lesser_Antilles">Impact in the Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Impact in the Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Windward_Islands">Windward Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Windward Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The outer <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">rainbands</a> of Maria produced heavy rainfall and strong gusts across the southern <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hewanorra_International_Airport" title="Hewanorra International Airport">Hewanorra</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_F._L._Charles_Airport" title="George F. L. Charles Airport">George F. L. Charles</a> airports of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> respectively recorded 4.33 in (110 mm) and 3.1 in (80 mm) of rain, though even higher quantities fell elsewhere on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Scattered rock slides, landslides and uprooted trees caused minor damage and blocked some roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stluciarock_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-stluciarock-79">[79]</a></sup> Several districts experienced localized blackouts due to downed or damaged power lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The agricultural sector, especially the banana industry, suffered losses from the winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stluciarock_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-stluciarock-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heavy rainfall amounting to 3–5 in (75–125 mm)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> caused scattered flooding across <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>; in <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Barbados" title="Christ Church, Barbados">Christ Church</a>, the flood waters trapped residents from the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Barbados#Towns.2C_villages.2C_and_hamlets" title="Christ Church, Barbados">Goodland</a> in their homes and inundated the business streets of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Gap" title="Saint Lawrence Gap">Saint Lawrence Gap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Maria stirred up rough seas that flooded coastal sidewalks in <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a> and damaged boats as operators had difficulties securing their vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> High winds triggered an island-wide power outage and downed a coconut tree onto a residence in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph,_Barbados" title="Saint Joseph, Barbados">Saint Joseph</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Passing 30 mi (50 km) off the northern shorelines, Maria brought torrential rainfall and strong gusts to Martinique but spared the island of its hurricane-force windfield,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchislands_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-87">[87]</a></sup> which at the time extended 25 mi (35 km) around the eye.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The commune of <a href="/wiki/Le_Marigot" title="Le Marigot">Le Marigot</a> recorded 6.7 inches (170 mm) of rain over a 24-hour period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rainfall_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-rainfall-89">[89]</a></sup> By September 19, Maria had knocked out power to 70,000 households, about 40% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lci_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-lci-90">[90]</a></sup> Water service was cut to 50,000 customers, especially in the communes of <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne-Rouge" title="Le Morne-Rouge">Le Morne-Rouge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gros-Morne,_Martinique" title="Gros-Morne, Martinique">Gros-Morne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchislands_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interieur_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-91">[91]</a></sup> Numerous roads and streets, especially along the northern coast, were impassible due to rock slides, fallen trees and toppled power poles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interieur_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lci_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-lci-90">[90]</a></sup> Streets in <a href="/wiki/Fort-de-France" title="Fort-de-France">Fort-de-France</a> were inundated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchislands_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-87">[87]</a></sup> In the seaside commune of <a href="/wiki/Le_Carbet" title="Le Carbet">Le Carbet</a>, rough seas washed ashore large rocks and demolished some coastal structures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frenchislands_87-3"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimescarib_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimescarib-92">[92]</a></sup> while some boats were blown over along the bay of the commune of <a href="/wiki/Sch%C5%93lcher" title="Schœlcher">Schœlcher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Martinique's agricultural sector suffered considerable losses: about 70% of banana crops sustained wind damage, with nearly every tree downed along the northern coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cropsfrench_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-cropsfrench-94">[94]</a></sup> There were no deaths on the island, although four people were injured in the hurricane—two seriously and two lightly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interieur_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau,_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg/290px-Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg/435px-Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg/580px-Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau%2C_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_part_of_Roseau,_the_capital_city_of_Dominica.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An aerial view of part of Roseau, revealing widespread damage to roofs. Flash floods clogged roads with debris, vegetative and structural, and mud.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rainfall ahead of the hurricane caused several landslides in Dominica as water levels across the island began to rise by the afternoon of September 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-before_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-before-95">[95]</a></sup> Maria made landfall at 21:15 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Standard_Time" title="Atlantic Standard Time">AST</a> that day (1:15 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>, September 19) as a Category 5 hurricane with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 160 mph (260 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominica_landfall_TCU_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dominica_landfall_TCU-20">[20]</a></sup> These winds, the most extreme to ever impact the island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> battered the roof of practically every home—including the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Dominica" title="Prime Minister of Dominica">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Skerrit" title="Roosevelt Skerrit">Roosevelt Skerrit</a>, who required rescue when his home began to flood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBtimes_PM_roof_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBtimes_PM_roof-97">[97]</a></sup> Downing all cellular, radio and internet services, Maria effectively cut Dominica off from the outside world; the situation there remained unclear for a couple of days after the hurricane's passage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimedom_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimedom-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Skerrit called the devastation "mind boggling" before going offline, and indicated immediate priority was to rescue survivors rather than assess damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimedom_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimedom-98">[98]</a></sup> Initial <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">ham radio</a> reports from the capital of <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> on September 19 indicated "total devastation," with half the city flooded, cars stranded, and stretches of residential area "flattened".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next morning, the first aerial footage of Dominica elucidated the scope of the destruction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominicafootage_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dominicafootage-101">[101]</a></sup> Maria left the mountainous country blanketed in a field of debris: Rows of houses along the entirety of the coastline were rendered uninhabitable, as widespread floods and landslides littered neighborhoods with the structural remnants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominicafootage_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dominicafootage-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debrisfield_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-debrisfield-102">[102]</a></sup> The hurricane also inflicted extensive damage to roads and public buildings, such as schools, stores and churches,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debrisfield_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-debrisfield-102">[102]</a></sup> and affected all of Dominica's 73,000 residents in some form or way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> The air control towers and terminal buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Canefield_Airport" title="Canefield Airport">Canefield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas%E2%80%93Charles_Airport" title="Douglas–Charles Airport">Douglas Charles</a> airports were severely damaged, although the runways remained relatively intact and open to emergency landings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> The disaster affected all of the island's 53 health facilities, including the badly damaged <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret_Hospital_(Roseau)" title="Princess Margaret Hospital (Roseau)">primary hospital</a>, compromising the safety of many patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominicafootage_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dominicafootage-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNreport_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNreport-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3336" data-file-width="5008" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A road in the <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> area is littered with structural debris, damaged vegetation and downed power poles and lines.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The infrastructure of Roseau was left in ruins; practically every power pole and line was downed, and the main road was reduced to fragments of flooded asphalt. The winds stripped the public library of its roof panels and demolished all but one wall of the Baptist church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> To the south of Roseau, riverside flooding and numerous landslides impacted the town of <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Michel" title="Pointe Michel">Pointe Michel</a>, destroying about 80% of its structures and causing most of the deaths in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pointemichel_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-pointemichel-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Outside the capital area, the worst of the destruction was concentrated around the east coast and rural areas, where collapsed roads and bridges isolated many villages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-2"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> The port and fishing town of <a href="/wiki/Marigot,_Dominica" title="Marigot, Dominica">Marigot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Andrew Parish, Dominica">Saint Andrew Parish</a>, was 80% damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Settlements in <a href="/wiki/Saint_David_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint David Parish, Dominica">Saint David Parish</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Castle_Bruce" title="Castle Bruce">Castle Bruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Good_Hope,_Dominica" title="Good Hope, Dominica">Good Hope</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Grand_Fond,_Dominica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grand Fond, Dominica (page does not exist)">Grand Fond</a>, had been practically eradicated; many homes hung off cliffs or decoupled from their foundations. In <a href="/wiki/Rosalie,_Dominica" title="Rosalie, Dominica">Rosalie</a>, rushing waters gushed over the village's bridge and damaged facilities in its bay area. Throughout <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick_Parish,_Dominica" title="Saint Patrick Parish, Dominica">Saint Patrick Parish</a>, the extreme winds ripped through roofs and scorched the vegetation. Buildings in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bay,_Dominica" title="Grand Bay, Dominica">Grand Bay</a>, the parish's main settlement, experienced total roof failure or were otherwise structurally compromised. Many houses in <a href="/wiki/La_Plaine,_Dominica" title="La Plaine, Dominica">La Plaine</a> caved in or slid into rivers, and its single bridge was broken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mariadominicareport_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-mariadominicareport-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Overall, the hurricane damaged the roofs of as much as 98% of the island's buildings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-3"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> including those serving as shelters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dominicafootage_101-3"><a href="#cite_note-Dominicafootage-101">[101]</a></sup> half of the houses had their frames destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-4"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> Its ferocious winds defoliated nearly all vegetation, splintering or uprooting thousands of trees and decimating the island's lush rainforests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The agricultural sector, a vital source of income for the country, was completely wiped out: 100% of banana and tuber plantations was lost, as well as vast amounts of livestock and farm equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcrossreport_103-5"><a href="#cite_note-redcrossreport-103">[103]</a></sup> In Maria's wake, Dominica's population suffered from an island-wide water shortage due to uprooted pipes. The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency">Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency</a> (CDEMA) estimates that the hurricane has caused "billions of dollars" worth of damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dominicadamage_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-dominicadamage-111">[111]</a></sup> As of October 1, there are 30 fatalities confirmed across the island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WT_death_toll_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-WT_death_toll-66">[66]</a></sup> with more than 50 reported missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Guadeloupe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_(nettoyage_des_routes).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3343" data-file-width="4394" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/220px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/330px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/440px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_(nettoyage_des_routes).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Numerous trees fell across Guadeloupe, clogging roadways with debris</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Blustery conditions spread over <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> as Maria tracked to the south of the archipelago, which endured hours of unabating hurricane-force winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The strongest winds blew along the southern coastlines of <a href="/wiki/Basse-Terre_Island" title="Basse-Terre Island">Basse-Terre Island</a>: <a href="/wiki/Gourbeyre" title="Gourbeyre">Gourbeyre</a> observed a peak wind speed of 101 mph (162 km/h), while winds up north in nearby <a href="/wiki/Baillif" title="Baillif">Baillif</a> reached 92 mph (148 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupemeteo_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupemeteo-114">[114]</a></sup> Along those regions, the hurricane kicked up extremely rough seas with 20 ft (6 m) waves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waves_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-waves-115">[115]</a></sup> The combination of rough seas and winds was responsible for widespread structural damage and flooding throughout the archipelago, especially from Pointe-à-Pitre, along <a href="/wiki/Grande-Terre" title="Grande-Terre">Grand-Terre Island</a>'s southwestern coast, to <a href="/wiki/Petit-Bourg" title="Petit-Bourg">Petit-Bourg</a> and the southern coasts on Basse-Terre Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-69">[69]</a></sup> Aside from wind-related effects, rainfall from Maria was also significant. In just a day, the hurricane dropped nearly a month's worth of rainfall at some important locations: <a href="/wiki/Pointe-%C3%A0-Pitre" title="Pointe-à-Pitre">Pointe-à-Pitre</a> recorded a 24-hour total of 7.5 inches (191 mm), while the capital of <a href="/wiki/Basse-Terre" title="Basse-Terre">Basse-Terre</a> measured 6.4 in (163 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rainfall_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-rainfall-89">[89]</a></sup> Even greater quantities fell at higher elevations of Basse Terre Island, with a maximum total of 18.07 in (459 mm) measured at the mountainous locality of <a href="/wiki/Matouba" title="Matouba">Matouba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Claude,_Guadeloupe" title="Saint-Claude, Guadeloupe">Saint-Claude</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupemeteo_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupemeteo-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the archipelago, the hurricane left 40% of the population (80,000 households) without power and 25% of landline users without service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-116">[116]</a></sup> The islands of <a href="/wiki/Marie-Galante" title="Marie-Galante">Marie-Galante</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a> and especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Les_Saintes" title="Les Saintes">Les Saintes</a> bore the brunt of the winds, which caused heavy damage to structures and nature alike and cut the islands off from their surroundings for several days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-116">[116]</a></sup> Homes on <a href="/wiki/Terre-de-Haut_Island" title="Terre-de-Haut Island">Terre-de-Haut Island</a> of Les Saintes were flooded or lost their roofs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> On the mainland, sections of Pointe-à-Pitre stood under more than 3.3 feet (1 m) of water, and the city's hospital sustained significant damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interieur_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-91">[91]</a></sup> The Basse-Terre region suffered severe damage to nearly 100% of its banana crops, comrpising a total area of more than 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acres</a> (2,000 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a>); farmers described the destruction to their plantations as "complete annihilation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cropsfrench_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-cropsfrench-94">[94]</a></sup> Beyond their impact on farmland, the strong winds ravaged much of the island's vegetation: fallen trees and branches covered practically every major road and were responsible for one death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_116-2"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-116">[116]</a></sup> Another person was killed upon being swept out to sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_69-4"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-69">[69]</a></sup> Two people disappeared at sea after their vessel capsized offshore <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a>, east of mainland <a href="/wiki/Grande-Terre" title="Grande-Terre">Grande-Terre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_116-3"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-116">[116]</a></sup> Damage from Maria across Guadeloupe amounted to at least €100 million (US$120 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dmgguadeloupe_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-dmgguadeloupe-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Virgin_Islands">United States Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United States Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Maria's outer eyewall was reported by the National Hurricane Center to have crossed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> while the hurricane was at Category 5 intensity. The hurricane caused extensive and severe damage to the island. Sustained winds at the <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Point_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge">Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge</a> reached 99 to 104 mph (159 to 167 km/h) and gusted to 137 mph (220 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The Luis Hospital suffered roof damage and flooding, but remained operational.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> One person died from a storm-induced heart attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StCroixHeartAttack_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-StCroixHeartAttack-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_in_the_Greater_Antilles_and_the_United_States">Impact in the Greater Antilles and the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Impact in the Greater Antilles and the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico_2">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Georges 1998</a></td>
<td>Jayuya</td>

<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene" title="Hurricane Irene">Irene 2011</a></td>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_(2017)_170923-H-NI589-0007_(36602415074).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_(2017)_170923-H-NI589-0007_(36602415074).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thousands of homes suffered varying degrees of damage while large swaths of vegetation were shredded by the hurricane's violent winds</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The storm made landfall on Puerto Rico on Wednesday, September 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT20170920_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT20170920-127">[127]</a></sup> A sustained wind of 64 mph (103 km/h) with a gust to 113 mph (182 km/h) was reported in San Juan, Puerto Rico, immediately prior to the hurricane making landfall on the island. After landfall, wind gusts of 109 mph (175 km/h) were reported at Yabucoa Harbor and 118 mph (190 km/h) at Camp Santiago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In addition, very heavy rainfall occurred throughout the territory, peaking at 37.9 in (962.7 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Widespread flooding affected San Juan, waist-deep in some areas, and numerous structures lost their roof.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT20170920_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT20170920-127">[127]</a></sup> The coastal <a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla neighborhood</a> of San Juan was largely destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o" title="Cataño">Cataño</a> saw extensive damage, with the Juana Matos neighborhood estimated to be 80 percent destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Sep21_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Sep21-131">[131]</a></sup> The primary airport in San Juan, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport">Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport</a>, was slated to reopen on September 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">Storm surge</a> and flash flooding—stemming from flood gate releases at <a href="/wiki/La_Plata_Lake" title="La Plata Lake">La Plata Lake</a> Dam—converged on the town of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, trapping thousands of residents. Survivors indicate that flood waters rose at least 6 ft (1.8 m) in 30 minutes, with flood waters reaching a depth of 15 ft (4.6 m) in some areas. More than 2,000 people were rescued once military relief reached the town 24 hours after the storm. At least eight people died due to the flooding while many are unaccounted for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ToaBaja_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-ToaBaja-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hurricane completely destroyed the island's power grid, leaving all 3.4 million residents without electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Sep21_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Sep21-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Puerto Rican governor <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rosselló">Ricardo Rosselló</a> stated that it could take months to restore power in some locations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> with San Juan Mayor <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Yul%C3%ADn_Cruz" title="Carmen Yulín Cruz">Carmen Yulín Cruz</a> estimating that some areas would remain without power for four to six months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Communication networks were crippled across the island. Ninety-five percent of cell networks were down with 48 of the island's 78 counties networks being completely inoperable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-134">[134]</a></sup> Eighty-five per cent of above-ground phone and internet cables were knocked out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Only one radio station, <a href="/wiki/WAPA_(AM)" title="WAPA (AM)">WAPA 680 AM</a>, remained on-air through the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_134-2"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_2" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_3" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm/854px--Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="31.801" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm/Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm.480p.webm" type="video/webm; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Maria at Coast Guard Sector San Juan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The nearby island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vieques" title="Vieques">Vieques</a> suffered similarly extensive damage. Communications were largely lost across the island. Widespread property destruction took place with many structures leveled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The recreational ship <i>Ferrel</i> carrying a family of four issued a distress signal while battling 20 ft (6.1 m) seas and 115 mph (185 km/h) winds on September 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferrel_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrel-140">[140]</a></sup> Communications with the vessel were lost near Vieques on September 20. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Royal_Navy" title="British Royal Navy">British Royal Navy</a> conducted search-and-rescue operations utilizing an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HC-130" title="HC-130">HC-130</a> aircraft, a fast response cutter, <a href="/wiki/USS_Kearsarge_(LHD-3)" title="USS Kearsarge (LHD-3)">USS <i>Kearsarge</i></a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RFA_Mounts_Bay" title="RFA Mounts Bay">RFA <i>Mounts Bay</i></a> and Navy helicopters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> On September 21, the mother and her two children were rescued while the father drowned inside the capsized vessel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ferrel_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrel-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maria's Category 4 winds broke a 96-foot (29 m) line feed antenna of the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">Arecibo Observatory</a>, causing it to fall 500 feet (150 m) and puncturing the dish below, greatly reducing its ability to function until repairs can be made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> On September 24, Governor Rosselló estimated that the damage from Hurricane Maria in Puerto Rico was surely over the $8 billion damage by Hurricane Georges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tallies_up_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-tallies_up-144">[144]</a></sup> Approximately 80 percent of the territory's agriculture was lost due to the hurricane, with losses estimated at $780 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> As of October 4, the death toll on Puerto Rico stood at 34,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consumerinfoline_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-consumerinfoline-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deathtollPR_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-deathtollPR-146">[146]</a></sup> however some expressed concern that the final death toll could be significantly higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hispaniola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Torrential rains and strong winds impacted the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> as Maria tracked northeast of the country. Assessments on September 22 indicate 110 homes were destroyed, 570 were damaged, and 3,723 were affected by flooding. Approximately 60,000 people lost power in northern areas of the country. Flooding and landslides rendered many roads impassable, cutting off 38 communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_Sep22_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC_Sep22-148">[148]</a></sup> Five people, all of them males, were killed in the Dominican Republic: four of them were of <a href="/wiki/Haitians_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Haitians in the Dominican Republic">Haitian origin</a>, killed when they were swept away by floodwaters; the fifth person was a Dominican man who died in a landslide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRfivedeaths_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-DRfivedeaths-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hurricane Maria center passed 250 km from Haiti northern coast but has received a large amount of rain and suffered some flooding. Three deaths were reported: a 45-year-old man died in the commune of Limbe, in the <a href="/wiki/Nord_(Haitian_department)" title="Nord (Haitian department)">department of the North</a>, while attempting to cross a flooded river. Two other people, a woman and a man, were mortally wounded in <a href="/wiki/Cornillon,_Ouest" title="Cornillon, Ouest">Cornillon</a>, a small town 40 kilometers east of the capital <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a>, according to the authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europe1_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-europe1-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland_United_States_2">Mainland United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mainland United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Maria brushed the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> on September 26 as the center of the storm passed by offshore and brought tropical storm conditions to the area along with a storm surge, large waves, and rip currents to the coast. The storm knocked out power to 800 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_Energy_Progress" title="Duke Energy Progress">Duke Energy Progress</a> customers in the <a href="/wiki/Havelock,_North_Carolina" title="Havelock, North Carolina">Havelock</a> area, with restoration of power expected to take several hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-4"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_North_Carolina_Power" title="Dominion North Carolina Power">Dominion North Carolina Power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras_Electric_Cooperative" title="Cape Hatteras Electric Cooperative">Cape Hatteras Electric Cooperative</a> experienced scattered power outages. Winds of 23 mph (37 km/h) and gusts of 41 mph (66 km/h) were reported at <a href="/wiki/Dare_County_Regional_Airport" title="Dare County Regional Airport">Dare County Regional Airport</a> at <a href="/wiki/Manteo,_North_Carolina" title="Manteo, North Carolina">Manteo</a> on September 27 while winds of 40 mph (64 km/h) were reported in <a href="/wiki/Duck,_North_Carolina" title="Duck, North Carolina">Duck</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver2_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver2-65">[65]</a></sup> Maria caused beach erosion at the ferry terminal at the north end of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocracoke_Island" title="Ocracoke Island">Ocracoke Island</a> that washed out a portion of the paved lanes where vehicles wait to board the ferry. By the morning of September 26, the storm flooded <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Highway_12" title="North Carolina Highway 12">North Carolina Highway 12</a> along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsobserver_64-5"><a href="#cite_note-newsobserver-64">[64]</a></sup> Rip currents from Maria caused three swimmers to drown and several others to be rescued at the <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Shore" title="Jersey Shore">Jersey Shore</a> on the weekend of September 23–24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> A fourth drowning death occurred in <a href="/wiki/Fernandina_Beach,_Florida" title="Fernandina Beach, Florida">Fernandina Beach, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica_2">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the destruction to thousands of homes, most supermarkets and the water supply system, many of Dominica's residents were in dire need of food, water and shelter for days in Maria's wake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debrisfield_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-debrisfield-102">[102]</a></sup> Through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Catastrophe_Risk_Insurance_Facility" title="Caribbean Catastrophe Risk Insurance Facility">Caribbean Catastrophe Risk Insurance Facility</a>, Dominica received approximately US$19.2 million in emergency funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS <i>Wasp</i></a>, previously deployed to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> to assist in relief efforts after Hurricane Irma, arrived in Dominica on September 22. The vessel carried two <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_SH-60_Seahawk" title="Sikorsky SH-60 Seahawk">Sikorsky SH-60 Seahawk</a> helicopters to assist in distribution of relief supplies in hard-to-reach areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> on September 23, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Skerrit" title="Roosevelt Skerrit">Roosevelt Skerrit</a> called the situation in Dominica an "international humanitarian emergency".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Navy" title="Royal Canadian Navy">Royal Canadian Navy</a> vessel <a href="/wiki/HMCS_St._John%27s" title="HMCS St. John's">HMCS <i>St. John's</i></a> was dispatched to Dominica<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> at the request of Dominican Prime Minister Skerrit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico_3">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This article documents a <b><a href="/wiki/Portal:Current_events" title="Portal:Current events">current disaster</a></b>. Information regarding it may change rapidly as more information becomes available; news reports and other primary sources may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources#Breaking_news" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">unreliable</a>. The <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=history">last updates</a> to this article <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Risk_disclaimer" title="Wikipedia:Risk disclaimer">may not reflect</a> the most current information about this disaster for all areas. <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
