<tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">There's a humanitarian emergency here in Puerto Rico.... This is an event without precedent.</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rosselló">Ricardo Rosselló</a>, Governor of Puerto Rico<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-156">[156]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The power grid was effectively destroyed by the hurricane, leaving millions without electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Power_grid_destroyed._157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Power_grid_destroyed.-157">[157]</a></sup> An economist estimated that Maria caused at least <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a> 50 billion in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-158">[158]</a></sup> As of September 26, 95% of the island was without power, less than half the population had potable water, and 95% of the island had no cell phone service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> There are ongoing fuel shortage and distribution problems, with 720 of 1100 gas stations open as of October 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guajataca_Lake" title="Guajataca Lake">Guajataca Dam</a> was structurally damaged, and on September 22, the National Weather Service issued a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_flood_emergency" title="Flash flood emergency">flash flood emergency</a> for parts of the area in response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Tens of thousands of people were ordered to evacuate the area, with about 70,000 thought to be at risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The entirety of Puerto Rico was declared a federal disaster zone shortly after the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-156">[156]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> planned to open an air bridge with three to four aircraft carrying essential supplies to the island daily starting on September 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_134-3"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-134">[134]</a></sup> Limited commercial traffic resumed at <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport">Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport</a> on September 22 under primitive conditions. A dozen commercial flights operated daily as of September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In marked contrast to the initial relief efforts for <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>, on September 22 the only signs of relief efforts were beleaguered Puerto Rican government employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-On_the_Ground.2C_A_Stunned_Start_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-On_the_Ground.2C_A_Stunned_Start-164">[164]</a></sup> The territory's government contracted 56 small companies to assist in restoring power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_156-2"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-156">[156]</a></sup> Eight FEMA Urban Search &amp; Rescue (US&amp;R) teams were deployed to assist in rescue efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="1024" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/310px-Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/465px-Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/620px-Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_at_night_before_and_after_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Comparison of lights at night in Puerto Rico before <i>(top)</i> and after <i>(bottom)</i> Hurricane Maria. Note: Lower image date should read 25 Sept. 2017</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 24, the <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Kearsarge_(LHD-3)" title="USS Kearsarge (LHD-3)">USS <i>Kearsarge</i></a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dock_landing_ship" title="Dock landing ship">dock landing ship</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Oak_Hill_(LSD-51)" title="USS Oak Hill (LSD-51)">USS <i>Oak Hill</i></a> under Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_W._Hughes" title="Jeffrey W. Hughes">Jeffrey W. Hughes</a> along with the 2,400 marines of <a href="/wiki/26th_Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="26th Marine Expeditionary Unit">26th Marine Expeditionary Unit</a> arrived to assist in relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPMoreHelp_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPMoreHelp-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S.26S_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-S.26S-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> By September 24, there were 13 United States Coast Guard ships deployed around Puerto Rico assisting in the relief and restoration efforts: the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Cutter" title="National Security Cutter">National Security Cutter</a> <a href="/wiki/USCGC_James_(WMSL-754)" title="USCGC James (WMSL-754)">USCGC <i>James</i></a>; the <a href="/wiki/Medium_endurance_cutter" title="Medium endurance cutter">medium endurance cutters</a> <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Diligence_(WMEC-616)" title="USCGC Diligence (WMEC-616)">USCGC <i>Diligence</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Forward_(WMEC-911)" title="USCGC Forward (WMEC-911)">USCGC <i>Forward</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Venturous_(WMEC-625)" title="USCGC Venturous (WMEC-625)">USCGC <i>Venturous</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Valiant_(WMEC-621)" title="USCGC Valiant (WMEC-621)">USCGC <i>Valiant</i></a>; the <a href="/wiki/Sentinel-class_cutter" title="Sentinel-class cutter">fast response cutters</a> <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Donald_Horsley" title="USCGC Donald Horsley">USCGC <i>Donald Horsley</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Heriberto_Hernandez_(WPC-1114)" title="USCGC Heriberto Hernandez (WPC-1114)">USCGC <i>Heriberto Hernandez</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Joseph_Napier_(WPC-1115)" title="USCGC Joseph Napier (WPC-1115)">USCGC <i>Joseph Napier</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Richard_Dixon_(WPC-1113)" title="USCGC Richard Dixon (WPC-1113)">USCGC <i>Richard Dixon</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Winslow_W._Griesser" title="USCGC Winslow W. Griesser">USCGC <i>Winslow Griesser</i></a>; the coastal patrol boat USCGC <i>Yellowfin</i>; and the seagoing buoy tenders <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Cypress_(WLB-210)" title="USCGC Cypress (WLB-210)">USCGC <i>Cypress</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Elm_(WLB-204)" title="USCGC Elm (WLB-204)">USCGC <i>Elm</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Federal aid arrived on September 25 with the reopening of major ports. Eleven cargo vessels collectively carrying 1.3 million liters of water, 23,000 cots, and dozens of generators arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Full operations at the ports of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayanilla" title="Guayanilla">Guayanilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tallaboa" title="Tallaboa">Tallaboa</a> resumed on September 25, while the ports of San Juan, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fajardo" title="Fajardo">Fajardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culebra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Culebra, Puerto Rico">Culebra</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayama" title="Guayama">Guayama</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vieques" title="Vieques">Vieques</a> had limited operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_Mobility_Command" title="Air Mobility Command">Air Mobility Command</a> has dedicated eight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-17_Globemaster" title="C-17 Globemaster">C-17 Globemaster</a> aircraft to deliver relief supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-2"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> The Air Force assisted the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> with air traffic control repairs to increase throughput capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-3"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Transportation_Command" title="United States Transportation Command">United States Transportation Command</a> has moved additional personnel and eight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army" title="U.S. Army">U.S. Army</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UH-60_Black_Hawk" title="UH-60 Black Hawk">UH-60 Black Hawk</a> helicopters from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Campbell,_Kentucky" title="Fort Campbell, Kentucky">Fort Campbell, Kentucky</a> to Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport to increase distribution capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-4"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">United States Army Corps of Engineers</a> deployed 670 personnel engaged in assessing and restoring the power grid; as of September 25, 83 generators were installed and an additional 186 generators were en route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-5"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> On September 26, the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_ship" title="Hospital ship">hospital ship</a> <a href="/wiki/USNS_Comfort_(T-AH-20)" title="USNS Comfort (T-AH-20)">USNS <i>Comfort</i></a> began preparations for deployment;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MilTImeHospital_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-MilTImeHospital-172">[172]</a></sup> and was expected to take a week to arrive in Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> As of September 26, agencies of the U.S. government have delivered 4 million meals, 6 million liters of water, 70,000 tarps and 15,000 rolls of roof sheeting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MilTImeHospital_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-MilTImeHospital-172">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> troops have been activated and deployed to Puerto Rico from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connecticut_National_Guard" title="Connecticut National Guard">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_National_Guard" title="Georgia National Guard">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iowa_National_Guard" title="Iowa National Guard">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois_National_Guard" title="Illinois National Guard">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_National_Guard" title="Kentucky National Guard">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri_National_Guard" title="Missouri National Guard">Missouri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_National_Guard" title="New York National Guard">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_National_Guard" title="Rhode Island National Guard">Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_National_Guard" title="Wisconsin National Guard">Wisconsin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Standing_water_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="650" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg/200px-Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg/300px-Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg/400px-Standing_water_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Standing_water_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_poses_health_risks_for_its_residents_more_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_devastated_the_island.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Standing water in <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce, Puerto Rico</a> more than a week after Hurricane Maria hit the island<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-175">[175]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 27, the Pentagon reopened two major airfields on Puerto Rico and started sending aircraft, specialized units, and a hospital ship to assist in the relief effort; Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Richard_C._Kim" title="Richard C. Kim">Richard C. Kim</a>, the deputy commanding general of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_North" title="United States Army North">United States Army North</a>, will be responsible for coordinating operations between the military, FEMA and other government agencies, and the private sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Massive amounts of water, food, and fuel have either been delivered to ports in Puerto Rico or are held up at ports in the mainland United States because there is a lack of trucker drivers to move the goods into the interior; the lack of communication networks has hindered the effort as only 20% of drivers have reported to work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> As of September 28, the Port of San Juan has only been able to dispatch 4% of deliveries received and has very little room to accept additional shipments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> As of September 28, 44 percent of the population remains without drinking water and the U.S. military is shifting from "a short term, sea-based response to a predominantly land-based effort designed to provide robust, longer term support" with fuel delivery a top priority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army194489_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Army194489-179">[179]</a></sup> A joint Army National Guard and Marine expeditionary unit (MEU) team has established an Installation Staging Base at the former <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Roads_Naval_Station" title="Roosevelt Roads Naval Station">Roosevelt Roads Naval Station</a>; they are transporting via helicopter Department of Health and Human Services assessment teams to hospitals across Puerto Rico to determine medical requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Army194489_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-Army194489-179">[179]</a></sup> On September 29, the <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a> <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS Wasp</a></i> which had been providing relief activities to the island of <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> was diverted to Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> As of September 30, FEMA official Alejandro de la Campa stated that 5% of electricity, 33% of the telecommunications infrastructure, and 50% of water services have been restored to the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Residents_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_line_up_at_an_ATM_in_hopes_of_getting_some_cash._More_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_struck,_residents_are_waiting_in_long_lines_to_withdraw_money_and_for_gasoline.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="1023" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Residents_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_line_up_at_an_ATM_in_hopes_of_getting_some_cash._More_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_struck%2C_residents_are_waiting_in_long_lines_to_withdraw_money_and_for_gasoline.jpg/200px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Residents_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_line_up_at_an_ATM_in_hopes_of_getting_some_cash._More_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_struck%2C_residents_are_waiting_in_long_lines_to_withdraw_money_and_for_gasoline.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Residents_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_line_up_at_an_ATM_in_hopes_of_getting_some_cash._More_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_struck%2C_residents_are_waiting_in_long_lines_to_withdraw_money_and_for_gasoline.jpg/400px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Residents_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_line_up_at_an_ATM_in_hopes_of_getting_some_cash._More_than_a_week_after_Hurricane_Maria_struck,_residents_are_waiting_in_long_lines_to_withdraw_money_and_for_gasoline.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
More than a week after Hurricane Maria struck, residents of <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce, Puerto Rico</a> wait in long lines at an ATM to withdraw cash. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-175">[175]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 28, 2017, Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_S._Buchanan" title="Jeffrey S. Buchanan">Jeffrey S. Buchanan</a> was dispatched to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> to lead all military hurricane relief efforts there and to see how the military can be more effective in the recovery effort, particularly in dealing with the thousands of containers of supplies that are stuck in port because of "red tape, lack of drivers, and a crippling power outage".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> On September 29 he stated that there were not enough troops and equipment in place but more would be arriving soon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>With centralized fossil-fuel-based power plants and grid infrastructure expected to be out of commission for weeks to months, some renewable energy projects are in the works, including the shipment of hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla</a> <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Powerwall" title="Tesla Powerwall">Powerwall</a> battery systems to be integrated with solar PV systems<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and Sonnen solar microgrid projects at 15 emergency community centers, the first expected to be completed in October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Virgin_Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: U.S. Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of September 25, the U.S. Coast Guard reports that the ports of Crown Bay, East Gregerie Channel, West Gregerie Channel, and Redhook Bay on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>; the ports of Krause Lagoon, Limetree Bay, and Frederiksted on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Croix, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Croix</a>, and the port of Cruz Bay on <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a> are open with restrictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-6"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> On September 25, 11 flights arrived with 200,000 meals, 144,000 liters of water, and tarps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FemaNewsSep25_165-7"><a href="#cite_note-FemaNewsSep25-165">[165]</a></sup> Troops have been activated and deployed to the U.S. Virgin Islands from the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_National_Guard" title="Virginia National Guard">Virginia National Guard</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_National_Guard" title="West Virginia National Guard">West Virginia National Guard</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Missouri_National_Guard" title="Missouri National Guard">Missouri National Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>, and UH-60 Blackhawk helicopters from the Tennessee Army National Guard.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_U.S._government_response">Criticism of U.S. government response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Criticism of U.S. government response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the immediate aftermath of Maria, the U.S. Department of Homeland Security (DHS) did not waive the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Marine_Act_of_1920" title="Merchant Marine Act of 1920">Jones Act</a> for Puerto Rico, which initially prevented the commonwealth from receiving any aid and supplies from non-U.S.-flagged vessels. This came in contrast to their waiving of the act following Hurricanes Harvey and Irma in Texas and Florida, respectively. A DHS Security spokesman said that there would be enough U.S. shipping for Puerto Rico, and that the limiting factors would be port capacity and local transport capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_0926_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_0926-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The act was waived for a period of ten days starting on September 28 following a formal request by Puerto Rico Governor Rosselló.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_Jones_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_Jones-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>San Juan Mayor <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Yul%C3%ADn_Cruz" title="Carmen Yulín Cruz">Carmen Yulín Cruz</a>, called the disaster a "terrifying humanitarian crisis" and pleaded for relief efforts to be sped up on September 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CruzQuote_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-CruzQuote-194">[194]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> contested claims that the administration was not responding effectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_0926_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_0926-195">[195]</a></sup> General <a href="/wiki/Joseph_L._Lengyel" title="Joseph L. Lengyel">Joseph L. Lengyel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_National_Guard_Bureau" title="Chief of the National Guard Bureau">Chief of the National Guard Bureau</a>, defended the Trump Administration's response, and reiterated that relief efforts were hampered by Puerto Rico being an island rather than on the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> responded to accusations that he does not care about Puerto Rico: "Puerto Rico is very important to me, and Puerto Rico -- the people are fantastic people. I grew up in New York, so I know many people from Puerto Rico. I know many Puerto Ricans. And these are great people, and we have to help them. The island is devastated."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 3rd, 2017, President Trump visited Puerto Rico. He compared the damage from Hurricane Maria to that of Hurricane Katrina, saying: "If you looked — every death is a horror, but if you look at a real catastrophe like Katrina, and you look at the tremendous hundreds and hundreds and hundreds of people that died, and you look at what happened here with really a storm that was just totally overbearing, nobody has seen anything like this (...) What is your death count as of this morning, 17?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Trump's remarks were widely criticized for implying that Hurricane Maria was not a "real catastrophe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> While in Puerto Rico, Trump also threw out some rolls of paper towels to crowds gathered at a relief shelter<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> and told the residents of the devastated island "I hate to tell you, Puerto Rico, but you've thrown our budget a little out of whack, because we've spent a lot of money on Puerto Rico".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.fema.gov/blog/2017-09-29/overview-federal-efforts-prepare-and-respond-hurricane-maria" rel="nofollow">Overview of Federal Efforts to Prepare for and Respond to Hurricane Maria</a> - activity summaries, graphic</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> in 1979 – one of the deadliest tropical cyclones to hit Dominica</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erika" title="Tropical Storm Erika">Tropical Storm Erika</a> in 2015 – devastated the island of Dominica with severe flooding</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a> in 1998 – the last major hurricane to strike Puerto Rico</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> in 1989 – the last Category 4 hurricane to strike Saint Croix</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in 1995 – brought severe damage to several islands of the Lesser Antilles</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">Hurricane Marilyn</a> in 1995 – affected Dominica and Guadeloupe and brought severe damage to the U.S. Virgin Islands</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hortense" title="Hurricane Hortense">Hurricane Hortense</a> in 1996 – affected Puerto Rico and caused widespread flooding across the island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1932_San_Ciprian_hurricane" title="1932 San Ciprian hurricane">1932 San Ciprian hurricane</a> – last hurricane to make landfall in Puerto Rico at Category 4 strength or higher.</li>
</ul>
